AUTHOR STATEMENT AND TRANSPARENCY DISCLOSURE  
The author conceived, designed, and wrote this specification. Generative AI tools (including OpenAI ChatGPT and Anthropic Claude) were used as drafting and consistency assistants. The author reviewed, verified, and edited all outputs and assumes full responsibility for the content, claims, and citations. This paper presents a theoretical framework. Empirical validation through pilots is planned but not yet completed. No operational deployment claims are made until validation studies are completed.

Maturity note. This specification is architecturally complete at the framework level for its declared release scope, but empirical validation, companion machine surfaces, and domain-specific measurement annexes remain active development priorities.

Historical release-delta details for v9.6.4, v9.6.5, v10.0-RC1, v10.0-RC2, v10.0, and v10.4 are retained in Appendix M. This front matter states the current v10.8 GitHub release posture only.

# v10.8 HUMAN PLATEAU / CMIU CALIBRATION AND SGP v5.5 SYNCHRONIZATION NOTICE

Release Delta (v10.5 → v10.6). This release integrates the Human Plateau / CMIU calibration clarification and synchronizes the Canon to SGP v5.5. It preserves the existing cascade architecture, equations, rights thresholds, TRC mechanics, Containment semantics, RLS formula, PLSS/FLGG architecture, HDW, PCC, RSP/RefStructRecord, Appendix AD scoring dictionary, and Tier 1-3 claim boundaries. It clarifies that the Human Plateau Rule is not species favoritism: human persons receive non-degradable protection, and humanity is the current evidenced plateau-class reality-managing community within the CMIU, while equivalent plateau extension remains open through SGP governed review.

Normative effect statement (v10.8). No intended change is made to the canonical admissibility cascade Reality Grounding → NCRC → TRC → Containment → RLS, rights coverage sets, TRC corridor mechanics, Containment semantics, RLS formula, PLSS/FLGG architecture, HDW, PCC, RSP/RefStructRecord, or Appendix AD. This release updates the SGP companion pin to SGP v5.5 and clarifies the human plateau / reality-management rationale without allowing any SGP scalar to weaken human protections, alter admissibility gates, or grant governance authority by itself.

Claim boundary table (Informative reading aid).

Release-boundary clarification (Normative).

“Architecturally complete,” “worked-run claimable,” “audit-ready,” “ProofPack-ready,” and “Tier 4-ready” are distinct statuses and MUST NOT be collapsed.

A framework may be architecturally complete without being empirically validated. A worked run may be claimable within its declared scope without the ecosystem being ProofPack-ready. Auditability surfaces may exist without a public replay validator. Tier 4 readiness remains prohibited until a public, independently replayable ProofPack exists.

Phase 1 release-boundary hardening (Normative clarification).

For public release interpretation, RippleLogic v10.8 is a conceptual/core-foundation and Tier 1-3 architectural specification within its declared scope. It is not an empirical validation claim, not a ProofPack-ready claim, not a Tier 4 claim, not a machine-verifiable-ecosystem-completeness claim, not a cross-domain validated UCI claim, not a legal-compliance certification, and not a deployment-readiness certification.

The phrase "ethical operating system" is a design-architecture claim. It SHALL NOT be read as a claim of universal cultural consent, lawful authority, empirical completion, automatic moral correctness, or permission to execute consequence-bearing decisions without the required governance authority and evidence.

UCI maturity boundary. UCI is structurally load-bearing as a diagnostic and tie-break interface, but empirically provisional until a published UCI Measurement Annex defines instruments, normalization rules, structural-independence checks, calibration procedure, and inter-rater reliability evidence. No v10.8 artifact may imply cross-domain validated UCI unless that annex and evidence are separately bundled and hash-pinned.

Admissibility vs permission (Normative clarification). Admissibility is a structural property determined by the cascade gates. Permission is a separate authorization act performed by an entity with appropriate authority. Compliance is a documentation property. A run that passes the cascade is admissible. An admissible run may still require permission, lawful authority, governance review, or domain-specific licensing before execution. A permitted run is not, by virtue of permission alone, admissible. RippleLogic determines admissibility; it does not grant permission, certify compliance, or substitute for lawful authority.

| **Claim type**                                  | Status in v10.8   | **Required condition**                                                                                                                  |
|-------------------------------------------------|-------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Tier 1-3 architectural completeness             | Claimable         | Defined by this canon and appendices for the declared release scope.                                                                    |
| Tier 3 run-level conformance                    | Claimable         | Run declares required inputs, satisfies tier minima, and emits a valid PCC.                                                             |
| Framework-level empirical operational-readiness | Not yet claimable | Requires empirical validation progress, including UCI measurement maturity and related evidence.                                        |
| Machine-verifiable ecosystem completeness       | Not yet claimable | Requires companion validator, schema, reference-calculator / registry surfaces, or equivalent ProofPack assets.                         |
| Tier 4 compliance                               | Prohibited        | No Tier-4 claim until ProofPack is publicly replayable and independently verified.                                                      |
| Cross-domain calibrated or validated UCI        | Prohibited        | Requires a published UCI Measurement Annex with named instruments, normalization rules, structural-independence evidence, and IRR data. |

Decision-state summary (Normative shorthand).

RippleLogic uses five distinct decision states that implementations MUST NOT collapse.

Rights-admissible = passes NCRC.

Admissible = passes NCRC and TRC.

Selectable = admissible and passes Containment in the applicable Containment mode.

Selected = chosen from the selectable set after RLS, tie-break, and any required escalation disposition.

Refusal = the framework cannot uniquely determine the applicable admissibility or selection state from declared inputs, evidence, projection rules, or layer commitments.

A later state MUST NOT be used to infer an earlier one, and no downstream score may rescue failure at an earlier state. Refusal MUST NOT be silently converted into gate failure, gate success, RLS tie-break, or discretionary selection. Refusal means the run lacks sufficient determination for the claim being attempted.

Execution Stability Diagnostic (v10.8 clarification). Execution stability is not a sixth decision state and not a replacement gate. It is a required diagnostic surface for Tier 2 and Tier 3 consequence-bearing execution, and recommended for medium- or high-stakes Tier 1 runs. It classifies the transition after hard admissibility and containment checks but before consequence-bearing execution. The diagnostic cannot rescue a failure at NCRC, TRC, or Containment, cannot convert Refusal into permission, and cannot use local stability to justify domination, rights infringement, or biosphere degradation.

CORE ARTIFACT ROLE MAP (release-line orientation)

\- RippleLogic_v10.8_Canon.docx: governing artifact, authoritative canonical byte-stream companion to the release manifest, and normative source of truth for this release line.

\- SGP v5.5: companion sentience / moral-status protocol. Authoritative for sentience-scoring procedures, scalar canon, plateau semantics, rights-of-protection scalar definitions, governed review requirements, and classification-stability cautions. RippleLogic consumes only SGP outputs through Appendix G and MUST NOT define or recompute SGP internals.

SGP split-roadmap boundary (Informative but release-controlling for interpretation).

Future SGP work SHOULD further separate moral patienthood, governance-participation readiness, and stewardship/power readiness as first-class outputs. v10.8 consumes only the pinned SGP scalar interface and MUST NOT infer governance authority, voting weight, office eligibility, or stewardship power from moral patienthood or rights-of-protection status.

This roadmap note does not change the v10.8 SGP binding interface. It prevents over-reading the current scalar as a pure sentience detector or as a governance-authority score.

\- ripple.md v3.6: portable alignment contract and assurance wrapper for implementations and deployments, including the wrapped-run ExecutionStabilityRecord field for high-stakes consequence-bearing episodes.

\- RippleLogic Agent System v10.8: deployment/control specification for agentic implementations under the current pinned companion line unless and until a later synchronized agent-system release is promoted.

\- Ripple Aligners Sheet v3.6: worked-run exemplar companion for replay, disclosure, and training, including the ExecutionStability sheet; not the repository-level validator or schema surface.

\- Machine-verifiable ecosystem completeness requires additional companion surfaces when claimed, including validator / schema / reference-calculator / registry artifacts or ProofPack assets beyond this core canon line.

\- Companion scalar-interface note: for SGP-integrated runs, RippleLogic treats SG_norm(E) and SG_patient_norm(E) as interface-stable outputs. Where provided by SGP v5.5 records, SG_measured_norm(E) and Plateau(E) MAY be logged for auditability, but RippleLogic MUST NOT infer plateau from raw measurement and MUST NOT substitute SG_measured_norm(E) for SG_norm(E) or SG_patient_norm(E) in normative computation. When SG_patient_norm(E) is available from the authoritative SGP record, RippleLogic SHOULD use SG_patient_norm(E) as the welfare-stream scalar for impacted protected stakeholders in residual welfare ranking. SGP-derived scalars MUST NOT be used to change admissibility outcomes under NCRC, TRC, or Containment.

## AC.1 Specification Contract (moved from front matter in v10.4)

# SECTION 0: SPECIFICATION CONTRACT (NORMATIVE)

## 0.1 Normative hierarchy (Single Source of Truth)

When interpreting RippleLogic v10.8, conflicts MUST be resolved using this precedence order (highest controls lowest):

1\. Main text rules explicitly labeled MUST, SHALL, or PROHIBITED

2\. Appendix B (Canonical Equations)

3\. Appendix C (Rights / NCRC Canon Pack)

4\. Appendix D (TRC and Scenario Governance Canon Pack)

5\. Appendix H (PCC and Audit Flags Canon Pack)

6\. Appendix AG (v10.8 Reality Grounding and Lean Cascade Patch)

7\. Appendix AH (Category Grounding and Primitive Audit Protocol)

8\. Appendix T (Execution Stability Diagnostic)

9\. Appendix U (Transition Admissibility and Evidence Substrate)

10\. Appendix AE (Layer-Discipline, Falsification, and Adaptive Reserve Addendum)

11\. Appendix AF (Decision Verdict Semantics, Projection Freeze, Closure Status, Falsification Classes, and Authority-Selection Separation)

12\. Appendix R (Tier 1-3 Reference Test Vectors)

13\. Appendix E (UCI Interface and Tier-3 Construction Guidance)

14\. Appendix G (SGP Integration Binding Interface)

15\. Appendix V (Measurement Maturity and Deployment Context Hardening)

16\. Appendix W (Schema Ownership, Registries, and Machine-Verifiable Surfaces)

17\. Appendix X (Reference Calculator, Machine Vectors, and ProofPack-Prep Roadmap)

18\. Appendix Y (Precision Patch: Legitimacy, Evidence Status, Validation, and Adoption Profiles)

19\. Appendix Z (Integration-Hardening Addendum)

20\. Appendix AA (Package-Content Boundary and Tooling-Line Separation)

21\. Appendix AB (Reference Structure Protocol)

22\. Appendix A (Symbols, Domains, and Notation Canon)

23\. Appendix N (Stewardship Pack Canon)

24\. Appendix F (Failure Modes and Anti-Gaming Controls)

25\. Appendix J (Pre-Registration Templates and Scoring Definitions)

26\. Appendix AD (49-Cell Welfare Dictionary): canonical interpretive reference for cell meanings, scoring language, and reviewer checks. Subordinate to Appendix B equations and to all normative gates; governs scoring interpretation and reviewer literacy only. It does not control admissibility, thresholds, or claim boundaries.

27\. Examples, templates, and illustrative values (non-normative; includes Appendix K unless a future version explicitly elevates a named subsection)

28\. Appendix O (Conformance Reference Map; informative pointer layer only)

Note (Informative). Version history and release notes are recorded in Appendix M and do not control normative meaning.

## 0.2 Tier contract and claims (v10.8 Canon line; Core Release 2026.07 package line) Tier 1-3: Executable in the v10.8 Canon release line, subject to stated minimum requirements. The Core Release 2026.07 package line contains Canon v10.8 / SGP v5.5 / ripple.md v3.6 / Agent System v10.8 / Primer v2.6 / Aligners Sheet v3.6. Any conformance claim against this release MUST pin to the v10.8 Canon artifact and the matching package manifest and hashes. Tier 4: PROHIBITED to claim in this release (design target only). Any Tier-4 content remains informational architecture describing what becomes claimable only after ProofPack publication and independent replayability.

## 0.3 Conformance vocabulary (Normative) RippleLogic uses distinct predicates; implementations MUST NOT collapse them.

- Rights-admissible: passes NCRC.

- Admissible: passes NCRC and TRC. Formally: Admissible(a) := NCRC(a) AND TRC(a).

- Selectable: admissible and passes Containment (Mode A).

- Selected: the final chosen option from the selectable set, either by ALLOW_FRAMEWORK_SELECTION when the framework selection path is decisive or by a separately disclosed AuthoritySelectionRecord when the framework refuses deterministic selection. A selected option MUST NOT be represented as a unique framework verdict when FrameworkVerdict is REFUSE_DETERMINISTIC_SELECTION.

## 0.4 Consolidated symbols and core objects (Normative; v10.8) Terminology note (Normative). In v10.8, u indexes Union Scopes (short: Scopes). “Union(s)” remains an allowed legacy narrative alias. This clarification SHALL NOT change the meaning of u or cascade semantics. Machine-readable surfaces SHOULD prefer UnionScope / UnionScopes as the canonical identifier family; Union remains a permitted human-readable alias in prose and UI text.

Table 0-1. Indices and core symbols

| **Symbol**   | **Meaning**                                     |
|--------------|-------------------------------------------------|
| u ∈ {1,…,7}  | Union Scope (Scope) index (legacy alias: union) |
| d ∈ {1,…,7}  | Dimension index                                 |
| a ∈ O        | Candidate option                                |
| s ∈ S        | Scenario index                                  |
| r ∈ R        | Right index                                     |
| k            | Impact instance index                           |
| g ∈ G\_{u,d} | Protected subgroup index (for rights checking)  |

Table 0-2. Core sets

| **Set**       | **Definition**                                               |
|---------------|--------------------------------------------------------------|
| U = {U₁,…,U₇} | Operational Scopes                                           |
| D = {D₁,…,D₇} | Welfare dimensions                                           |
| R             | Rights set: {LIFE, BODY, LBTY, NEED, DIGN, PROC, INFO, ECOL} |
| C_r ⊆ U×D     | Rights coverage sets                                         |
| C_cat ⊆ U×D   | Catastrophe cell set for TRC                                 |

Table 0-3. Welfare impact objects (all options a)

| **Symbol**      | **Meaning**                         | **Range** |
|-----------------|-------------------------------------|-----------|
| I_dir(u,d,a)    | Direct impact (post-saturation)     | \[-1,+1\] |
| I_prop(u,d,a)   | Propagated impact (post-saturation) | \[-1,+1\] |
| I_rights(u,d,a) | Rights worst-off subgroup impact    | \[-1,+1\] |

Table 0-4. Kernel, weights, and tail-risk symbols

| **Symbol**    | **Meaning**                   | **Constraint / Notes**                                                    |
|---------------|-------------------------------|---------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| K ∈ ℝ^{49×49} | Ripple kernel matrix (sparse) | Convention: K\_{ij} maps source j to target i (target-row, source-column) |
| w_u           | Union weights                 | w_u ≥ 0, Σ_u w_u = 1                                                      |
| v_d           | Dimension weights             | v_d ≥ 0, Σ_d v_d = 1                                                      |
| m(u,d)        | Applicability mask            | m ∈ {0,1} (RLS aggregation only)                                          |
| p_s           | Scenario probabilities        | p_s ≥ 0, Σ_s p_s = 1                                                      |
| ω_c           | Catastrophe weights           | ω_c ≥ 0, Σ\_{c∈C_cat} ω_c = 1                                             |
| α             | CVaR tail level               | α ∈ (0,1)                                                                 |
| τ_TRC         | Corridor threshold            | τ_TRC ∈ (0,1\]                                                            |

Table 0-5. Structural metrics

| **Symbol** | **Meaning**                                 | **Range** |
|------------|---------------------------------------------|-----------|
| UCI_u      | Union Coherence Index for scope u           | \[0,1\]   |
| ΔUCI_u(a)  | UCI_u(a) − UCI_u(baseline)                  | \[-1,+1\] |
| HOI        | Hollowing-Out Index (monitoring diagnostic) | unbounded |

## 0.5 Version commitments (Normative; v10.8) The canonical welfare impact scale is \[-1,+1\] with Baseline-Zero Rule (Section 5). Optional UI scale conversion (non-normative): If a user interface uses a percent-like scale, map the canonical cell impact I(u,d,a) ∈ \[-1,+1\] to UI points via: points = 100 × I. All admissibility gates (NCRC, TRC, Containment) and RLS calculations MUST be performed on the canonical \[-1,+1\] scale, or be converted back exactly before computation. Tier 1-3 TRC uses bounded-impact loss (Section 8). Tier 4 is design target only; no Tier-4 claims permitted until ProofPack is publicly replayable. UCI Equity for Self (U₁): E₁ := 1 by definition. The equity component is fixed at 1 for Self because equity-as-distribution does not apply within a single individual. This provides a neutral, non-penalizing identity value. UCI for Self is computed from Cohesion, Flow, and Resilience with E₁ = 1. UCI Equity for Biosphere (U₇): E₇ := 1 by default unless a governed biosphere-equity instrument is declared for the run. This provides a neutral, non-penalizing identity value when distributional equity is not operationalized for the Biosphere union. Record E7_METHOD_FIXED_1_DEFAULT (or the declared instrument identifier) in PCC.

Patch-line interpretation (Normative clarification). Unless a rule explicitly names a more specific patch version, references in section headings, appendix titles, or release notes to the current release line SHALL be interpreted as applying to the v10.8 line. Patch releases in the current release line MUST preserve the cascade architecture unless an explicit versioned change states otherwise.

## 0.6 Single Canonical Artifact Rule (Normative; v10.8)

This document is the single canonical RippleLogic Foundation Paper for v10.8. Any copy labeled “final,” “regen,” “patched,” “draft,” “fork,” or similar is non-canonical unless it is byte-identical to this artifact. Implementations, manifests, validators, ProofPacks, and downstream specifications MUST pin to the canonical artifact (filename + hash in the release manifest) and MUST NOT treat variant text as authoritative.

Retirement clause (Normative). Any earlier artifacts later labeled v10.8 that are not byte-identical to this canonical artifact are RETIRED and MUST NOT be used as sources of truth for v10.8 interpretation or for any v10.8 compliance claim.

Integrity note (Informative). The canonical hash MUST be published in a sibling release manifest rather than embedded in the document body, because any edit changes the byte stream.

Canonical byte-stream designation (Normative). Unless a release manifest explicitly states otherwise, the DOCX file for this Foundation Paper is the authoritative canonical byte stream for v10.8. Any PDF distributed with the release is a derived render for reading and review, not the controlling byte stream.

## 0.8 Release Packaging and Integrity Manifests (Informative)

Recommended release bundle (Informative). Publish (i) the canonical DOCX/PDF, (ii) a SHA-256 manifest file (for example, RippleLogic\_\<version\>.sha256) listing hashes for each artifact, (iii) a machine-readable release manifest when available (for example YAML), and (iv) optional signatures. The manifest is the stable anchor for byte identity, while the document remains human-readable and editable without self-referential hashing issues. To avoid self-reference problems, a checksum manifest SHOULD hash the release artifacts and MAY omit its own file unless a separate detached signature or higher-level release record governs it.

# APPENDIX AD: 49-CELL WELFARE DICTIONARY (CANONICAL INTERPRETIVE REFERENCE)

Tooling warning (Normative for implementation). Tooling MUST source rights coverage from Section 7.2 / Appendix C.2 and catastrophe cells from Section 8.2, never from Appendix AD icons. Appendix AD icons are interpretive cues, not machine-authoritative gate definitions.

Status and boundaries. Appendix AD is the canonical interpretive reference for welfare-cell meanings, baseline-relative scoring language, evidence literacy, and reviewer checks. It is binding for interpreting what each Scope × Dimension cell is about. Its examples, indicator lists, and gate-relevance tags are illustrative and non-exhaustive. Appendix AD does not modify the cascade, equations, NCRC, TRC, Containment, RLS, UCI/HOI, HDW, SGP, PCC, RSP/RefStructRecord, thresholds, or claim boundaries. Gate tags are contextual cues for evaluators, not automated verdicts; admissibility is determined only by running the full cascade against declared evidence in the governed system.

The welfare matrix is the surface RLS ranks on: seven union scopes (U1–U7) × seven welfare dimensions (D1–D7), giving forty-nine accountability domains. Each cell is scored on a canonical −1 to +1 scale, relative to a declared baseline. A cell score is a claim, not a vibe: it asserts what changes, for whom, how strongly, on what evidence, and under what uncertainty.

Scale. +1 strong benefit, +0.5 moderate benefit, 0 no material change from baseline — never “unknown”, −0.5 moderate harm, −1 severe harm. Where an impact is not known, the cell is marked unknown, disclosed, and escalated where gate-relevant.

Ordering. Welfare scoring is the last step, not the first. The cascade is sequenced as Reality Grounding → NCRC → TRC → Containment → RLS — and an option is ranked across these cells only after it has cleared the rights, tail-risk, and containment gates. No welfare score rescues an option that failed an earlier gate.

Gate-relevance key. Tags below indicate where a cell may become relevant to a gate in a real run; they are contextual cues, not fixed classifications, and do not replace a canonical evaluation. Canonical rights coverage set C_r and declared catastrophe cell set C_cat, not the icon labels alone, control non-maskability and gate status.

⚖ Rights-relevance cue — may require NCRC review when the cell lies in the canonical or governed rights coverage set C_r, or when the PCC declares a rights-relevant extension. The canonical C_r, not this icon alone, controls rights-covered status and non-maskability.

⚠ Tail-risk relevance cue — may require TRC review when the cell lies in the declared catastrophe cell set C_cat, or when catastrophe relevance is otherwise triggered. The declared C_cat and TRC trigger rules, not this icon alone, control catastrophe-cell status and non-maskability.

⛓ Containment-relevant — a local gain may degrade the wider scopes the decision depends on; checked before RLS.

◌ Ordinary welfare — ranked by RLS once the gates are cleared.

? Uncertain — evidence weak or contested; mark, disclose, and escalate if gate-relevant.

<tr class="odd">
<td colspan="7"><strong>U1 Self</strong></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U1/D1</strong></p>
<p><strong>Personal Resources</strong></p>
<p><em>label: personal resources</em></p></td>
<td>An individual's economic security: income, savings, housing stability, and access to the material means of a decent life.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> More stable income, affordable housing, reduced debt, secured access to essentials.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Job loss, eviction risk, debt spirals, loss of essential goods or services.</p></td>
<td>income and employment records; housing stability / eviction data; debt and arrears; cost-of-living and benefit uptake</td>
<td><p><strong>◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Ordinary welfare in most cases; can escalate to rights-covered where a subsistence or social-minimum floor is legally recognised.</em></p></td>
<td>A wage policy that lifts low-income workers above a local living-wage line improves U1/D1.</td>
<td>A reviewer checks whether the income/housing change is measured against a declared baseline cohort, not anecdote.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p><strong>U1/D2</strong></p>
<p><strong>Personal Health</strong></p>
<p><em>label: personal health</em></p></td>
<td>The individual's physical and mental health, safety, and bodily integrity.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Lower injury/illness risk, better access to care, improved mental health, safer conditions.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Injury, illness, untreated conditions, exposure to hazards, deteriorating mental health.</p></td>
<td>morbidity / mortality data; care access and waiting times; injury and exposure records; validated mental-health measures</td>
<td><p><strong>⚖ Rights ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Frequently rights-covered: bodily integrity and access-to-care floors can trigger NCRC. Severe individual harm escalates regardless of aggregate benefit.</em></p></td>
<td>A treatment-access change that removes a barrier for a chronic-illness group improves U1/D2.</td>
<td>A reviewer asks whether a claimed health gain rests on outcome data or only on inputs (e.g. clinics built ≠ health improved).</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U1/D3</strong></p>
<p><strong>Relationships</strong></p>
<p><em>label: relationships</em></p></td>
<td>The quality and stability of a person's close personal relationships and social connection.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Stronger bonds, reduced isolation, more supportive networks.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Isolation, relationship breakdown, forced separation, loss of support.</p></td>
<td>loneliness / connection surveys; support-network mapping; separation or displacement records</td>
<td><p><strong>◌ Ordinary ? Uncertain</strong></p>
<p><em>Usually ordinary welfare; measurement is often soft, so uncertainty should be marked explicitly.</em></p></td>
<td>A relocation program that keeps support networks intact protects U1/D3.</td>
<td>A reviewer challenges whether a relationship claim is evidenced or inferred from a proxy like attendance.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p><strong>U1/D4</strong></p>
<p><strong>Learning</strong></p>
<p><em>label: learning</em></p></td>
<td>The individual's access to education, skills, and the capacity to learn and develop.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Better access to learning, skill gains, expanded opportunity.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Lost access to education, deskilling, barriers to learning.</p></td>
<td>enrolment and completion; skills assessments; access and dropout data</td>
<td><p><strong>◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Ordinary welfare; can touch rights where a basic-education entitlement exists.</em></p></td>
<td>A reskilling program for displaced workers improves U1/D4.</td>
<td>A reviewer asks whether learning outcomes are demonstrated or only opportunity offered.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U1/D5</strong></p>
<p><strong>Personal Agency</strong></p>
<p><em>label: autonomy</em></p></td>
<td>The person's real ability to choose, refuse, consent, act, and shape their own life path.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> More autonomy, better options, stronger consent, freedom from coercion and surveillance.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Coercion, manipulation, surveillance, forced dependency, loss of meaningful choice.</p></td>
<td>consent quality; availability of alternatives / opt-out; coercion complaints; mobility and accessibility data; applicable legal protections</td>
<td><p><strong>⚖ Rights ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Often rights-covered. Triggers NCRC when liberty, bodily integrity, due process, dignity, or information rights are impaired — non-compensatory regardless of welfare gains elsewhere.</em></p></td>
<td>A transport policy that gives disabled residents reliable independent mobility improves U1/D5.</td>
<td>A reviewer tests whether consent was genuine and revocable, or merely formal.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p><strong>U1/D6</strong></p>
<p><strong>Purpose</strong></p>
<p><em>label: purpose</em></p></td>
<td>The individual's sense of meaning, dignity, and worth in their life and work.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Greater sense of purpose, recognition, dignity, and self-respect.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Humiliation, alienation, loss of role or recognition, indignity.</p></td>
<td>dignity / recognition measures; role and identity surveys; qualitative testimony</td>
<td><p><strong>⚖ Rights ? Uncertain</strong></p>
<p><em>Can be rights-covered where human dignity is implicated; otherwise ordinary. Often hard to measure — mark uncertainty.</em></p></td>
<td>A program that treats welfare recipients with dignified, non-stigmatising processes supports U1/D6.</td>
<td>A reviewer distinguishes a genuine dignity effect from sentiment unsupported by experience data.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U1/D7</strong></p>
<p><strong>Local Conditions</strong></p>
<p><em>label: local conditions</em></p></td>
<td>The immediate physical environment a person lives in: air, noise, water, hazards, and surroundings.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Cleaner air/water, less noise, fewer local hazards, healthier surroundings.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Pollution exposure, noise, contamination, environmental hazards near the person.</p></td>
<td>local air/water/noise monitoring; hazard proximity; exposure records</td>
<td><p><strong>◌ Ordinary ⚖ Rights</strong></p>
<p><em>Ordinary welfare; can become rights-covered under environmental-health protections and disproportionate-exposure (environmental-justice) concerns.</em></p></td>
<td>A factory buffer-zone rule that cuts a household's pollutant exposure improves U1/D7.</td>
<td>A reviewer checks measured exposure change against the affected location, not a city-wide average.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td colspan="7"><strong>U2 Household</strong></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U2/D1</strong></p>
<p><strong>Household Resources</strong></p>
<p><em>label: household resources</em></p></td>
<td>The economic security of the household unit: shared income, assets, housing, and ability to meet needs.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Improved household finances, housing security, reduced shared debt.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Household impoverishment, housing loss, debt, inability to meet needs.</p></td>
<td>household income and assets; housing tenure; arrears and food-security data</td>
<td><p><strong>◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Ordinary welfare; escalates toward rights where dependents (children, disabled members) face a subsistence floor.</em></p></td>
<td>A childcare subsidy that frees household income improves U2/D1.</td>
<td>A reviewer asks whether the household, not just the earner, is the measured unit.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p><strong>U2/D2</strong></p>
<p><strong>Household Health</strong></p>
<p><em>label: household health</em></p></td>
<td>The collective physical and mental health and safety of household members, including dependents.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Better shared health, safer home, improved care for dependents and caregivers.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Household illness, unsafe housing, caregiver burnout, harm to dependents.</p></td>
<td>household health surveys; home-safety inspections; caregiver-strain measures; dependent outcome data</td>
<td><p><strong>⚖ Rights ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Frequently rights-covered where children or dependents are affected; child welfare can trigger NCRC. Caregiver harm is easily hidden — surface it.</em></p></td>
<td>A home-care support program that reduces caregiver strain and improves a dependent's health raises U2/D2.</td>
<td>A reviewer checks that dependents and caregivers are scored separately, not blended into one household figure.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U2/D3</strong></p>
<p><strong>Family Cohesion</strong></p>
<p><em>label: family cohesion</em></p></td>
<td>The strength, stability, and supportive quality of relationships within the household.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Stronger family bonds, stability, reduced conflict, kept-together units.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Family breakdown, forced separation, household conflict, instability.</p></td>
<td>family-stability surveys; separation / removal records; conflict indicators</td>
<td><p><strong>⚖ Rights ◌ Ordinary ? Uncertain</strong></p>
<p><em>Can be rights-covered (family unity, child rights); otherwise ordinary. Measurement is soft — mark uncertainty.</em></p></td>
<td>A policy that avoids unnecessary family separation in housing transitions protects U2/D3.</td>
<td>A reviewer asks whether a cohesion claim rests on outcomes or on assumed effects of a program.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p><strong>U2/D4</strong></p>
<p><strong>Shared Learning</strong></p>
<p><em>label: shared learning</em></p></td>
<td>The household's collective access to information, education, and learning capacity.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Better shared access to education and information, intergenerational learning.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Loss of household educational access, information poverty.</p></td>
<td>household connectivity / device access; children's schooling continuity; adult-learning access</td>
<td><p><strong>◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Ordinary welfare; touches rights where basic-education entitlements for children apply.</em></p></td>
<td>A home-broadband program that enables children's remote schooling improves U2/D4.</td>
<td>A reviewer checks access actually reaches the household, not just the area.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U2/D5</strong></p>
<p><strong>Household Agency</strong></p>
<p><em>label: household agency</em></p></td>
<td>The household's collective ability to make decisions, plan, and control its own circumstances.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Greater household self-determination, planning ability, freedom from external control.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Loss of household control, externally imposed decisions, dependency.</p></td>
<td>decision-autonomy surveys; dependency / conditionality of support; forced-relocation data</td>
<td><p><strong>⚖ Rights ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Can be rights-covered (family privacy, autonomy); otherwise ordinary.</em></p></td>
<td>A flexible-benefit design that lets households allocate support to their own priorities raises U2/D5.</td>
<td>A reviewer tests whether household choice is real or constrained by conditions.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p><strong>U2/D6</strong></p>
<p><strong>Family Meaning</strong></p>
<p><em>label: family meaning</em></p></td>
<td>The household's shared sense of identity, belonging, dignity, and purpose.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Stronger shared identity, belonging, dignity, and continuity.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Loss of household identity, stigma, indignity, eroded belonging.</p></td>
<td>belonging / identity surveys; stigma indicators; qualitative testimony</td>
<td><p><strong>? Uncertain ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Usually ordinary welfare; can touch dignity rights. Soft to measure — mark uncertainty.</em></p></td>
<td>A culturally-respectful resettlement process preserves U2/D6.</td>
<td>A reviewer separates a real meaning effect from program rhetoric.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U2/D7</strong></p>
<p><strong>Home Environment</strong></p>
<p><em>label: home environment</em></p></td>
<td>The physical environmental quality of the home and its immediate setting.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Healthier home conditions, reduced indoor hazards, better surroundings.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Indoor pollution, mould, hazards, degraded immediate environment.</p></td>
<td>housing-quality inspections; indoor air / damp measures; hazard records</td>
<td><p><strong>◌ Ordinary ⚖ Rights</strong></p>
<p><em>Ordinary welfare; rights-relevant under habitability standards.</em></p></td>
<td>A retrofit program that removes household mould improves U2/D7.</td>
<td>A reviewer checks measured home conditions, not self-report alone.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td colspan="7"><strong>U3 Community</strong></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U3/D1</strong></p>
<p><strong>Local Resources</strong></p>
<p><em>label: local resources</em></p></td>
<td>The shared economic resources, infrastructure, and services available to a local community.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Better local infrastructure, services, and economic opportunity.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Loss of services, infrastructure decay, local economic decline.</p></td>
<td>local service provision; infrastructure condition; local employment / business data</td>
<td><p><strong>◌ Ordinary ⛓ Containment</strong></p>
<p><em>Ordinary welfare; containment-relevant when local gains are extracted at the cost of wider scopes, or when shared infrastructure is hollowed out.</em></p></td>
<td>A community facility upgrade that adds usable shared services improves U3/D1.</td>
<td>A reviewer asks whether the benefit is genuinely shared or captured by a subgroup.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p><strong>U3/D2</strong></p>
<p><strong>Community Health</strong></p>
<p><em>label: public health</em></p></td>
<td>The collective physical and mental health and safety of the local population.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Lower community disease/injury burden, better local care access, safer environment.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Local disease spread, unsafe conditions, reduced care access, environmental health harm.</p></td>
<td>local public-health surveillance; care-access data; injury / safety statistics; environmental-health monitoring</td>
<td><p><strong>⚖ Rights ⚠ Tail-risk ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Ordinary welfare normally; rights-relevant under disproportionate harm or care-access floors; tail-relevant where local outbreaks or contamination could cascade.</em></p></td>
<td>A clean-water intervention that cuts a community's disease burden improves U3/D2.</td>
<td>A reviewer checks whether subgroup harms are masked by a favourable community average.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U3/D3</strong></p>
<p><strong>Community Cohesion</strong></p>
<p><em>label: trust and cohesion</em></p></td>
<td>The quality of trust, cooperation, belonging, safety, and relational fabric within a community.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Increased trust, reduced isolation, better cooperation, stronger neighbourhood resilience.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Polarisation, exclusion, displacement, fear, social fragmentation.</p></td>
<td>community trust surveys; participation rates; crime / fear-of-crime data; displacement records</td>
<td><p><strong>⛓ Containment ⚖ Rights ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Containment-relevant because eroded social fabric degrades the wider system; rights-relevant if discrimination, exclusion, or targeted domination appears.</em></p></td>
<td>A public-space renovation that increases safe cross-group interaction improves U3/D3.</td>
<td>A reviewer asks whether cohesion gains for some came via exclusion of others.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p><strong>U3/D4</strong></p>
<p><strong>Local Knowledge</strong></p>
<p><em>label: local knowledge</em></p></td>
<td>The community's shared knowledge, information access, and local expertise.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Better local information access, preserved local/Indigenous knowledge, stronger civic literacy.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Information loss, erosion of local knowledge, misinformation spread.</p></td>
<td>information-access measures; local-knowledge preservation records; misinformation prevalence</td>
<td><p><strong>⛓ Containment ◌ Ordinary ? Uncertain</strong></p>
<p><em>Ordinary welfare; containment-relevant where an epistemic commons is degraded. Can be rights-relevant for Indigenous knowledge.</em></p></td>
<td>A program documenting local ecological knowledge with community consent improves U3/D4.</td>
<td>A reviewer checks consent and ownership of the knowledge claimed as preserved.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U3/D5</strong></p>
<p><strong>Community Agency</strong></p>
<p><em>label: community agency</em></p></td>
<td>The community's collective capacity to organise, participate, and influence decisions affecting it.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Stronger local voice, participation, self-organisation, and contestability.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Disenfranchisement, suppressed organising, exclusion from decisions.</p></td>
<td>participation in local governance; consultation quality; association / assembly freedom</td>
<td><p><strong>⚖ Rights ⛓ Containment ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Often rights-covered (assembly, association, participation); containment-relevant where civic capacity underpins system stability.</em></p></td>
<td>A binding community-consultation requirement on local development raises U3/D5.</td>
<td>A reviewer tests whether participation was substantive or a procedural formality.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p><strong>U3/D6</strong></p>
<p><strong>Shared Meaning</strong></p>
<p><em>label: shared meaning</em></p></td>
<td>The community's shared identity, culture, dignity, and sense of collective purpose.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Stronger shared identity, cultural continuity, pride, and belonging.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Cultural erosion, stigma, loss of identity, collective humiliation.</p></td>
<td>cultural-participation data; heritage continuity; community-identity surveys</td>
<td><p><strong>⚖ Rights ? Uncertain ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Ordinary welfare; rights-relevant for cultural rights and minority protection. Soft to measure — mark uncertainty.</em></p></td>
<td>Protecting a culturally significant site during redevelopment preserves U3/D6.</td>
<td>A reviewer separates a genuine cultural effect from a symbolic gesture.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U3/D7</strong></p>
<p><strong>Local Ecology</strong></p>
<p><em>label: local ecology</em></p></td>
<td>The ecological condition of the community's local environment: green space, biodiversity, water, land.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Restored habitat, cleaner local environment, protected green space.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Habitat loss, local pollution, degraded green space, contamination.</p></td>
<td>local biodiversity / green-space data; pollution monitoring; land-use change</td>
<td><p><strong>⛓ Containment ⚠ Tail-risk ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Containment-relevant (local ecology supports wider systems); tail-relevant where degradation is irreversible or contamination could cascade.</em></p></td>
<td>A watershed-protection rule that prevents local contamination improves U3/D7.</td>
<td>A reviewer asks whether 'no local effect' was measured or merely assumed.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td colspan="7"><strong>U4 Organization</strong></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U4/D1</strong></p>
<p><strong>Organizational Resources</strong></p>
<p><em>label: operating resources</em></p></td>
<td>An organization's operating means: finances, capital, staffing, and capacity to function and deliver.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Stronger finances, capacity, staffing, and operational sustainability.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Insolvency risk, capacity loss, layoffs, operational decline.</p></td>
<td>financial statements; staffing and capacity data; service-delivery metrics</td>
<td><p><strong>◌ Ordinary ⛓ Containment</strong></p>
<p><em>Ordinary welfare; containment-relevant when organizational gains are extracted by externalising harm onto community, polity, or biosphere scopes.</em></p></td>
<td>A funding change that stabilises a hospital's operating budget improves U4/D1.</td>
<td>A reviewer checks whether the organizational gain creates uncosted externalities in other cells (the classic 'operating resources up, U7 down' trap).</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p><strong>U4/D2</strong></p>
<p><strong>Organizational Safety</strong></p>
<p><em>label: safety</em></p></td>
<td>The safety of people within and affected by the organization: workers, users, and the public.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Fewer injuries, safer operations, better safety culture and compliance.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Workplace injury, unsafe products/services, public-safety incidents.</p></td>
<td>incident and injury rates; safety-compliance audits; near-miss reporting</td>
<td><p><strong>⚖ Rights ⚠ Tail-risk ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Rights-covered via labour and safety protections; tail-relevant where failure could cause catastrophic or mass-casualty events.</em></p></td>
<td>A maintenance regime that cuts industrial-accident rates improves U4/D2.</td>
<td>A reviewer checks whether reported safety reflects outcomes or only paperwork compliance.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U4/D3</strong></p>
<p><strong>Organizational Culture</strong></p>
<p><em>label: culture</em></p></td>
<td>The internal relational health of the organization: trust, fairness, inclusion, and cooperation.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Healthier culture, fairer treatment, reduced harassment, stronger cooperation.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Toxic culture, discrimination, harassment, low trust, burnout.</p></td>
<td>staff-climate surveys; grievance and turnover data; fairness / inclusion measures</td>
<td><p><strong>⚖ Rights ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Ordinary welfare; rights-relevant where discrimination or harassment occurs.</em></p></td>
<td>An anti-harassment reform that reduces verified grievances improves U4/D3.</td>
<td>A reviewer asks whether culture data is independent or self-reported by leadership.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p><strong>U4/D4</strong></p>
<p><strong>Knowledge Systems</strong></p>
<p><em>label: knowledge systems</em></p></td>
<td>The organization's knowledge, data integrity, institutional memory, and learning systems.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Better knowledge retention, data integrity, transparency, and learning.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Knowledge loss, data corruption, opacity, broken institutional memory.</p></td>
<td>data-integrity audits; documentation completeness; knowledge-retention metrics</td>
<td><p><strong>⛓ Containment ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Ordinary welfare; containment-relevant where degraded knowledge systems undermine accountability or wider-system reliability.</em></p></td>
<td>A records-integrity upgrade that makes decisions auditable improves U4/D4.</td>
<td>A reviewer tests whether claimed integrity is verifiable or asserted.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U4/D5</strong></p>
<p><strong>Role Agency</strong></p>
<p><em>label: role agency</em></p></td>
<td>The meaningful autonomy, voice, and fair treatment of individuals in their organizational roles.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> More voice, fair process, reasonable autonomy, freedom from arbitrary treatment.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Arbitrary power, suppressed voice, exploitation, loss of role autonomy.</p></td>
<td>worker-voice mechanisms; grievance outcomes; autonomy / discretion measures</td>
<td><p><strong>⚖ Rights ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Rights-relevant via labour rights and freedom of association; otherwise ordinary.</em></p></td>
<td>A grievance process with real remedy improves U4/D5.</td>
<td>A reviewer checks whether voice mechanisms produce outcomes or are decorative.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p><strong>U4/D6</strong></p>
<p><strong>Mission Coherence</strong></p>
<p><em>label: mission coherence</em></p></td>
<td>The alignment between the organization's stated purpose and its actual conduct and effects.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Stronger purpose-conduct alignment, integrity, and legitimate mission delivery.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Mission drift, purpose-washing, hollow mandate, loss of legitimacy.</p></td>
<td>mission-vs-outcome analysis; stakeholder-trust measures; conduct audits</td>
<td><p><strong>⛓ Containment ◌ Ordinary ? Uncertain</strong></p>
<p><em>Ordinary welfare; containment-relevant where mission decay (HOI-adjacent) hollows out the institution. Distinct from the formal HOI diagnostic.</em></p></td>
<td>A governance reform that realigns conduct with mandate improves U4/D6.</td>
<td>A reviewer asks whether coherence is evidenced by conduct or only by restated values.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U4/D7</strong></p>
<p><strong>Operational Footprint</strong></p>
<p><em>label: operational footprint</em></p></td>
<td>The environmental impact of the organization's operations: emissions, waste, resource use, land.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Lower emissions/waste, reduced resource intensity, smaller harmful footprint.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Pollution, emissions, waste, resource depletion, ecological damage.</p></td>
<td>emissions and waste data; resource-use intensity; environmental-compliance records</td>
<td><p><strong>⛓ Containment ⚠ Tail-risk ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Containment-relevant (footprint degrades wider scopes); tail-relevant where the footprint contributes to irreversible or large-scale harm. The canonical 'local win, wider loss' cell.</em></p></td>
<td>A process change that cuts a plant's emissions while sustaining output improves U4/D7.</td>
<td>A reviewer checks footprint against measured externalities, not offset claims alone.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td colspan="7"><strong>U5 Polity</strong></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U5/D1</strong></p>
<p><strong>Public Resources</strong></p>
<p><em>label: public resources</em></p></td>
<td>The polity's fiscal and material capacity: public finances, infrastructure, and provisioning.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Sounder public finances, better infrastructure, sustainable provisioning.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Fiscal crisis, infrastructure decay, depleted public capacity.</p></td>
<td>public-finance data; infrastructure condition indices; fiscal-sustainability metrics</td>
<td><p><strong>◌ Ordinary ⛓ Containment</strong></p>
<p><em>Ordinary welfare; containment-relevant where short-term fiscal wins erode long-term public capacity.</em></p></td>
<td>An infrastructure-maintenance program that prevents asset decay improves U5/D1.</td>
<td>A reviewer checks whether gains are sustainable or borrowed from the future.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p><strong>U5/D2</strong></p>
<p><strong>Population Health</strong></p>
<p><em>label: population health</em></p></td>
<td>The health, safety, and mortality outcomes of the whole population within a polity.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Lower population mortality/morbidity, better system-wide care, stronger resilience.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Rising mortality, system overload, reduced care access, public-health crises.</p></td>
<td>population mortality / morbidity; health-system capacity; health-equity gaps; outbreak surveillance</td>
<td><p><strong>⚠ Tail-risk ⚖ Rights ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Tail-relevant for pandemic / health-system-collapse scenarios (non-averagable); rights-relevant under right-to-health floors; otherwise ordinary welfare.</em></p></td>
<td>A vaccination program that lowers population mortality improves U5/D2.</td>
<td>A reviewer checks whether worst-case scenarios were bounded with a tail measure, not averaged away.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U5/D3</strong></p>
<p><strong>Legitimacy</strong></p>
<p><em>label: legitimacy</em></p></td>
<td>The rule of law, due process, accountability, and perceived legitimacy of public institutions.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Stronger rule of law, due process, accountability, and institutional trust.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Erosion of rule of law, impunity, corruption, collapse of institutional trust.</p></td>
<td>rule-of-law indices; due-process / judicial-independence measures; corruption indicators; institutional-trust surveys</td>
<td><p><strong>⛓ Containment ⚖ Rights ⚠ Tail-risk ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Strongly containment-relevant: legitimacy is load-bearing for the whole system. Rights-relevant (due process); tail-relevant where collapse risks systemic instability.</em></p></td>
<td>A judicial-independence safeguard that resists political capture improves U5/D3.</td>
<td>A reviewer tests whether legitimacy is measured independently or claimed by the institution being assessed.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p><strong>U5/D4</strong></p>
<p><strong>Information Access</strong></p>
<p><em>label: information access</em></p></td>
<td>The polity's information environment: access, transparency, free expression, and epistemic integrity.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Better transparency, information access, free expression, healthier epistemic commons.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Censorship, opacity, disinformation, surveillance chilling, epistemic capture.</p></td>
<td>transparency / FOI metrics; press-freedom indices; disinformation prevalence; surveillance scope</td>
<td><p><strong>⚖ Rights ⛓ Containment ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Rights-covered (free expression, information rights); containment-relevant because a damaged epistemic commons undermines all other governance.</em></p></td>
<td>An open-data and FOI reform that increases verifiable transparency improves U5/D4.</td>
<td>A reviewer checks whether transparency is real and usable or nominal.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U5/D5</strong></p>
<p><strong>Civil Agency</strong></p>
<p><em>label: civil agency</em></p></td>
<td>People's ability to participate in public life, exercise rights, contest authority, and influence governance.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Stronger voting access, participation, transparency, due process, and contestability.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Suppression, censorship, corruption, procedural exclusion, arbitrary enforcement, reduced civic voice.</p></td>
<td>voting access and turnout; procedural-fairness measures; availability of legal remedies; consultation quality; censorship reports</td>
<td><p><strong>⚖ Rights ⛓ Containment ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Frequently rights-covered: tied to due process, liberty, information, dignity, and civic rights — non-compensatory under NCRC. Containment-relevant for system stability.</em></p></td>
<td>A reform expanding access to public hearings raises U5/D5; one that blocks lawful dissent harms it.</td>
<td>A reviewer tests whether civic participation is enforceable or merely nominal, and whether any group is selectively excluded.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p><strong>U5/D6</strong></p>
<p><strong>Public Meaning</strong></p>
<p><em>label: public meaning</em></p></td>
<td>Shared civic identity, dignity, social contract, and non-domination across the polity.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Stronger civic dignity, inclusion, fair recognition, and a credible social contract.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Domination, civic humiliation, exclusionary identity, eroded social contract.</p></td>
<td>inclusion / recognition measures; social-contract trust surveys; discrimination indicators</td>
<td><p><strong>⚖ Rights ⛓ Containment ? Uncertain</strong></p>
<p><em>Rights-relevant (dignity, non-domination, non-discrimination); containment-relevant where a fractured social contract destabilises the polity. Soft to measure.</em></p></td>
<td>A reconciliation policy that credibly extends recognition to a marginalised group improves U5/D6.</td>
<td>A reviewer separates symbolic recognition from changes people actually experience.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U5/D7</strong></p>
<p><strong>Public Environment</strong></p>
<p><em>label: public environment</em></p></td>
<td>The environmental quality and ecological sustainability managed at the polity scale.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Better regional environmental quality, sustainable resource management, reduced systemic pollution.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Regional pollution, resource depletion, ecosystem degradation, environmental injustice.</p></td>
<td>regional environmental monitoring; resource-stock data; pollution and emissions; environmental-justice mapping</td>
<td><p><strong>⚠ Tail-risk ⛓ Containment ⚖ Rights ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Tail-relevant where regional harm is irreversible or large-scale; containment-relevant; rights-relevant under environmental-justice and environmental-rights regimes.</em></p></td>
<td>A regional emissions cap that prevents airshed degradation improves U5/D7.</td>
<td>A reviewer checks whether environmental-justice distribution was assessed, not just regional totals.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td colspan="7"><strong>U6 Humanity / CMIU</strong></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U6/D1</strong></p>
<p><strong>Global Resources</strong></p>
<p><em>label: global resources</em></p></td>
<td>Humanity's shared material base: global resource stocks, critical supply chains, and common infrastructure.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> More sustainable global resource use, resilient supply chains, protected commons.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Resource depletion, supply-chain fragility, degradation of global commons.</p></td>
<td>global resource-stock data; supply-chain resilience metrics; commons-condition indicators</td>
<td><p><strong>⛓ Containment ⚠ Tail-risk ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Containment-relevant and tail-relevant where depletion or fragility threatens systemic, hard-to-reverse harm at civilisational scale.</em></p></td>
<td>A critical-minerals stewardship agreement that reduces depletion risk improves U6/D1.</td>
<td>A reviewer checks whether 'global' claims rest on global data or extrapolated local figures.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p><strong>U6/D2</strong></p>
<p><strong>Human Safety</strong></p>
<p><em>label: human safety</em></p></td>
<td>The safety and survival of humanity at large, including existential and catastrophic risk.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Reduced catastrophic and existential risk; stronger global safety and resilience.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Increased existential, pandemic, conflict, or technological catastrophic risk.</p></td>
<td>catastrophic-risk assessments; biosecurity / nuclear-risk indicators; conflict-escalation data</td>
<td><p><strong>⚠ Tail-risk ⚖ Rights ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Primarily tail-relevant: catastrophic and existential risk is non-averagable and bounded under TRC, never traded against ordinary welfare. Rights-relevant at the right-to-life floor.</em></p></td>
<td>A biosecurity protocol that lowers engineered-pandemic risk improves U6/D2.</td>
<td>A reviewer checks that tail risk was bounded with a worst-case measure and not diluted by expected-value framing.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U6/D3</strong></p>
<p><strong>Cooperation</strong></p>
<p><em>label: cooperation</em></p></td>
<td>The capacity of humanity to coordinate, cooperate, and maintain peaceful, stable relations at scale.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Stronger global cooperation, conflict reduction, durable coordination institutions.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Breakdown of cooperation, arms races, institutional collapse, escalating conflict.</p></td>
<td>international-cooperation indices; conflict / treaty-compliance data; coordination-institution health</td>
<td><p><strong>⛓ Containment ⚠ Tail-risk ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Containment-relevant (cooperation underpins global stability); tail-relevant where breakdown risks large-scale conflict.</em></p></td>
<td>A verification regime that sustains an arms-control treaty improves U6/D3.</td>
<td>A reviewer asks whether cooperation is durable or a fragile short-term arrangement.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p><strong>U6/D4</strong></p>
<p><strong>Civilizational Knowledge</strong></p>
<p><em>label: civilizational knowledge</em></p></td>
<td>Humanity's accumulated knowledge, science, and the integrity and safety of its knowledge systems.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Knowledge preservation, scientific progress, epistemic integrity, responsible knowledge stewardship.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Knowledge loss, scientific capture, epistemic collapse, or proliferation of dangerous knowledge.</p></td>
<td>scientific-integrity measures; knowledge-preservation status; research-governance indicators</td>
<td><p><strong>⛓ Containment ⚠ Tail-risk ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Containment-relevant; tail-relevant in two directions — catastrophic loss of knowledge, and dangerous diffusion of harmful capability.</em></p></td>
<td>An open-but-governed research framework that preserves integrity while limiting dangerous diffusion improves U6/D4.</td>
<td>A reviewer checks whether knowledge benefits were weighed against misuse and proliferation pathways.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U6/D5</strong></p>
<p><strong>Collective Agency</strong></p>
<p><em>label: collective agency</em></p></td>
<td>Humanity's capacity for self-determination and legitimate collective decision-making at the species scale.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Stronger legitimate global agency, fair representation, and self-determination.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Concentration of unaccountable power, disenfranchisement of peoples, loss of collective self-determination.</p></td>
<td>representation / participation in global governance; power-concentration indicators; self-determination measures</td>
<td><p><strong>⚖ Rights ⛓ Containment ? Uncertain</strong></p>
<p><em>Rights-relevant (self-determination); containment-relevant where illegitimate concentration destabilises the system. Measurement is contested — mark uncertainty.</em></p></td>
<td>A governance reform giving affected populations real voice in a global regime improves U6/D5.</td>
<td>A reviewer tests whether 'collective' agency includes the marginalised or only powerful actors.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p><strong>U6/D6</strong></p>
<p><strong>Shared Purpose</strong></p>
<p><em>label: shared purpose</em></p></td>
<td>Humanity's shared sense of meaning, moral direction, and long-term orientation toward flourishing.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Stronger shared purpose, long-term orientation, intergenerational responsibility.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Nihilism, short-termism, loss of shared direction, intergenerational betrayal.</p></td>
<td>long-term-orientation indicators; intergenerational-equity measures; qualitative analysis</td>
<td><p><strong>? Uncertain ⛓ Containment ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Mostly ordinary/aspirational; containment-relevant where short-termism erodes long-term stability. Inherently soft — mark uncertainty and avoid overclaiming.</em></p></td>
<td>A long-horizon institution (e.g. a future-generations commissioner) can support U6/D6.</td>
<td>A reviewer flags this cell as especially prone to rhetoric and demands concrete mechanisms.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U6/D7</strong></p>
<p><strong>Planetary Conditions</strong></p>
<p><em>label: planetary conditions</em></p></td>
<td>The condition of planetary systems that support human civilisation and coordinated managing intelligence.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Reduced emissions, improved climate stability, lower systemic ecological risk, stronger global resilience.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Increased climate risk, global pollution, destabilised food/water systems, irreversible planetary degradation.</p></td>
<td>emissions data; climate models; planetary-boundary metrics; global food/water-security projections</td>
<td><p><strong>⚠ Tail-risk ⛓ Containment ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Often catastrophe-relevant: may trigger TRC where irreversible or large-scale harm is plausible. Containment-relevant as a system-stability check.</em></p></td>
<td>A high-emissions infrastructure choice may harm U6/D7 even when it benefits a local economy (U3/D1 or U4/D1).</td>
<td>A reviewer checks whether irreversibility and worst-case bounds were modelled, not just expected outcomes.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td colspan="7"><strong>U7 Biosphere</strong></td>
</tr>
<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U7/D1</strong></p>
<p><strong>Life-Support Resources</strong></p>
<p><em>label: life-support resources</em></p></td>
<td>The biosphere's foundational resources that sustain life: soil, fresh water, clean air, fertility.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Protected or restored soil, water, and air; sustained natural-resource base.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Soil loss, water depletion, air degradation, exhaustion of life-support systems.</p></td>
<td>soil-health data; freshwater-stock and quality; air-quality baselines; resource-renewal rates</td>
<td><p><strong>⚠ Tail-risk ⛓ Containment ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Tail-relevant where depletion is irreversible or threatens collapse of life-support systems; containment-relevant. Distinct from U4/D1 'operating resources'.</em></p></td>
<td>An aquifer-protection rule that prevents irreversible groundwater loss improves U7/D1.</td>
<td>A reviewer checks whether renewal rates, not just current stocks, were assessed.</td>
</tr>
<tr class="odd">
<td><p><strong>U7/D2</strong></p>
<p><strong>Ecosystem Health</strong></p>
<p><em>label: ecosystem health</em></p></td>
<td>The health, function, and viability of ecosystems and the species within them.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Healthier, functioning ecosystems; recovering species and habitats.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Ecosystem dysfunction, species decline, habitat collapse, trophic breakdown.</p></td>
<td>ecosystem-function indicators; species-population trends; habitat-condition assessments</td>
<td><p><strong>⚠ Tail-risk ⛓ Containment ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Tail-relevant where collapse or extinction is plausible and irreversible; containment-relevant as ecosystems underpin wider scopes.</em></p></td>
<td>A fisheries policy that lets a collapsing stock recover improves U7/D2.</td>
<td>A reviewer checks whether ecosystem-function evidence exists or only a single charismatic indicator.</td>

<tr class="even">
<td><p><strong>U7/D3</strong></p>
<p><strong>Biotic Relations</strong></p>
<p><em>label: biotic relations</em></p></td>
<td>The integrity of relationships and interdependencies among living systems and between humans and nature.</td>
<td><p><strong>+</strong> Restored ecological relationships, sustainable human-nature interactions, protected interdependencies.</p>
<p><strong>−</strong> Disrupted food webs, broken ecological relationships, harmful human-nature dynamics.</p></td>
<td>trophic / food-web indicators; interaction-network data; human-impact assessments</td>
<td><p><strong>⛓ Containment ⚠ Tail-risk ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>
<p><em>Containment-relevant: a local win that severs ecological relationships can fail containment even with strong U4/D1 gains; tail-relevant where cascades are plausible.</em></p></td>
<td>A factory expansion that damages a watershed may fail containment via U7/D3 even while improving U4/D1.</td>
<td>A reviewer asks whether relational/cascade effects were modelled or ignored as 'no direct effect'.</td>
</tr>

<p><em>label: ecological knowledge</em></p></td>
<td>Humanity's understanding and monitoring of ecological systems, including baseline and early-warning data.</td>

<p><strong>−</strong> Monitoring gaps, lost baselines, ecological ignorance, blind spots before thresholds.</p></td>

<td><p><strong>⛓ Containment ? Uncertain ◌ Ordinary</strong></p>

<td>Restoring wetland buffers that absorb flood shocks improves U7/D5.</td>
<td>A reviewer asks whether proximity to thresholds was assessed, not just current condition.</td>

<td>A factory expansion that damages a watershed may fail containment even when it improves U4/D1.</td>
<td>A reviewer checks whether integrity is evidenced by ecosystem-level data or inferred from a single metric.</td>
